{"code":1,"isDone":false,"toInsertArticleList":[{"createdTime":"2021-04-03 12:49:03","updatedTime":"2021-04-03 12:49:03","title":"‘Bridgerton’ Star Regé-Jean Page Will Not Return for Season 2","link":"https://www.slashfilm.com/?p=665264","description":"<p><img class=\"alignnone size-medium wp-image-665269 aligncenter\" src=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/Bridgerton-season-2-700x300.jpg\" alt=\"Bridgerton season 2\" width=\"700\" height=\"300\" srcset=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/Bridgerton-season-2.jpg 700w, https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/Bridgerton-season-2-360x154.jpg 360w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 700px) 100vw, 700px\" /></p>\n<p>Actor <strong>Regé-Jean Page</strong>, who burned up the screen in Netflix&#8217;s widely watched romance drama <strong><em>Bridgerton</em></strong>, will not be returning in the second season.</p>\n<p>This may come as a shock to viewers who haven&#8217;t looked into the origins of the series or read anything about its upcoming plans, but book readers have known about this from the beginning. <em>Bridgerton</em> will essentially take an anthology approach, with each planned season covering the events of one of author Julia Quinn&#8217;s novels, which focus on a different member of the titular family. Confirmation about Page not being a part of <em>Bridgerton</em> season 2 came from the show&#8217;s official Instagram account.<br />\n<span id=\"more-665264\"></span></p>\n<p><img class=\"alignnone size-medium wp-image-665266 aligncenter\" src=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/Bridgerton-insta-700x513.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"700\" height=\"513\" srcset=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/Bridgerton-insta.jpg 700w, https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/Bridgerton-insta-360x264.jpg 360w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 700px) 100vw, 700px\" /></p>\n<p>&#8220;One of the things that is different about this [romance] genre is that the audience knows the arc completes,&#8221; Page, who had only signed on for a one-season arc, told Variety. &#8220;They come in knowing that, so you can tie people in emotional knots because they have that reassurance that we&#8217;re going to come out and we&#8217;re going to have the marriage and the baby.&#8221;</p>\n<p>During his initial discussions with producer <strong>Shonda Rhimes</strong> about the role, he found it interesting that he could come in, contribute his part, &#8220;and then the Bridgerton family rolls on,&#8221; he said, saying that the idea of his one-season appearance &#8220;felt like a limited series.&#8221;</p>\n<p>&#8220;I have nothing but excitement for <em>Bridgerton</em> continuing to steam train off and conquer the globe,&#8221; he went on. &#8220;But there is also value in completing these arcs and sticking the landing.&#8221; In an Instagram post, the actor called his experience on the show &#8220;beyond anything I could have imagined.&#8221;</p>\n<p><img class=\"alignnone size-medium wp-image-665267 aligncenter\" src=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/Bridgerton-insta-2-700x447.jpg\" alt=\"\" width=\"700\" height=\"447\" srcset=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/Bridgerton-insta-2.jpg 700w, https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/Bridgerton-insta-2-360x230.jpg 360w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 700px) 100vw, 700px\" /></p>\n<p>Bridgerton season 2 will focus on the events of the second book in Quinn&#8217;s series, &#8220;The Viscount Who Loved Me,&#8221; and follow the oldest Bridgerton child, Anthony (<strong>Jonathan Bailey</strong>) as he embarks upon his own journey for love. The Daphne character (portrayed by <strong>Phoebe Dynevor</strong>) will be back for season 2 after marrying Page&#8217;s character, the Duke of Hastings, but the Duke will not appear in season. There&#8217;s a chance he could pop back up again in future seasons, though, as the lives of these familial characters intersect and cross over.</p>\n<p>Page will soon be seen in a <a href=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/new-dungeons-and-dragons-movie-cast-adds-rege-jean-page/\">new <em>Dungeons and Dragons</em> movie</a>, and Netflix subscribers will see him on that service again when <a href=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/the-gray-man-cast-rege-jean-page-billy-bob-thornton-alfre-woodard/\">he appears</a> in the Russo Brothers&#8217; spy thriller <em>The Gray Man</em> along with Ryan Gosling, Chris Evans, Ana de Armas, and more.</p>\n<p>The post <a rel=\"nofollow\" href=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/bridgerton-season-2-rege-jean-page/\">&#8216;Bridgerton&#8217; Star Regé-Jean Page Will Not Return for Season 2</a> appeared first on <a rel=\"nofollow\" href=\"https://www.slashfilm.com\">/Film</a>.</p>\n<div class=\"feedflare\">\n<a +0000","feedId":21,"bgimg":"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/Bridgerton-season-2-700x300.jpg","linkMd5":"f1615b06ca000e7afbc585cd95f8c3ed","bgimgJsdelivr":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx1/cdn22@2020_6/2021/04/03/04-49-08-367_505edda874d86092.webp","destWidth":700,"destHeight":300,"sourceBytes":56221,"destBytes":41872,"author":"Ben Pearson","articleImgCdnMap":{"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/Bridgerton-season-2-700x300.jpg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx1/cdn22@2020_6/2021/04/03/04-49-08-367_505edda874d86092.webp","https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/Bridgerton-insta-700x513.jpg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx10/cdn75@2020_2/2021/04/03/04-50-10-690_9852b09baa8cc73c.webp","https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/Bridgerton-insta-2-700x447.jpg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx32/cdn48@2020_2/2021/04/03/04-50-10-660_fbbf467e69008a69.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/slashfilm?d=yIl2AUoC8zA":null,"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/slashfilm?i=9ZN7IWqqp1Q:oAWx98YunPk:V_sGLiPBpWU":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx/cdn76@2020_1/2021/04/03/04-50-10-666_e79fe50b9b2f8fd3.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/slashfilm?d=I9og5sOYxJI":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx24/cdn57@2020_5/2021/04/03/04-50-11-348_879c5505f034c3d2.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/slashfilm?i=9ZN7IWqqp1Q:oAWx98YunPk:EGzC5_Ws_ZE":null,"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~r/slashfilm/~4/9ZN7IWqqp1Q":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx16/cdn63@2020_4/2021/04/03/04-50-10-531_2eeb2a4679a2608b.webp"},"publishedOrCreatedDate":1617425343645},{"createdTime":"2021-04-03 12:49:03","updatedTime":"2021-04-03 12:49:03","title":"How the Hilarious, Chilling World of ‘Made For Love’ Came to Life [Interview]","link":"https://www.slashfilm.com/?p=665165","description":"<p><img class=\"size-medium wp-image-665204 aligncenter\" src=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/Made-for-Love-Interview-700x300.jpeg\" alt=\"\" width=\"700\" height=\"300\" srcset=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/Made-for-Love-Interview.jpeg 700w, https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/Made-for-Love-Interview-360x154.jpeg 360w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 700px) 100vw, 700px\" /></p>\n<p><strong><em>Made for Love</em></strong> is a television show set in the near-future, but it&#8217;s about the here and now. A woman escaping from an abusive relationship. A tech mogul with too much power and not enough humanity. A general sense of chaos and an awareness that the world is always on the verge of a total meltdown. Sometimes, all we can do is laugh through the pain and the series does just that – the tinges of horror and the big science fiction ideas are always balanced by surreal, riotous comedy and a stunning lead performance from <strong>Cristin Milioti</strong>.</p>\n<p><a href=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/made-for-love-review/\">I loved the first episode</a> of <em>Made for Love</em> when it premiered at SXSW. And I loved the additional three episodes, which were sent to me ahead of my interview with showrunner <strong>Christina Lee</strong>, director <strong>Stephanie Laing</strong>, and writer/executive producer <strong>Alissa Nutting</strong> (who also wrote the book on which the series is based). I sat down with all three of them over Zoom to chat about the series, how it balances comedy with genre storytelling, how the cast brings their oddball characters to life, and whether or not there are already plans for a second season.</p>\n<p>The first three episodes of <em>Made for Love</em> are streaming now on HBO Max. Additional episodes will arrive weekly.</p>\n<p><span id=\"more-665165\"></span></p>\n<p class=\"p1\"><b>This is the best first episode of something I’ve seen in a while. And the opening minutes – within five minutes, I’m in. Can you talk about the idea of dropping us into this weird, wild world immediately?</b></p>\n<p class=\"p1\"><strong>Lee:</strong> Yeah, I feel like that came about really in the editing process. We had considered several different ways to start the show. What we knew that we wanted was to feel like you’re on a ride right away and that there’s a lot of information coming at you and this is exciting and you’re seeing these different worlds and filling in the holes along the way. With that intention, I think in the editing room we really saw how we wanted to start the show and that sort of informed more of the writing and directing as we went forward because we were able to shoot a few episodes before we shut down for the pandemic. During that time, we went back and said, “What’s something we want to see here in the pilot episode that we now have the luxury of thinking of and writing and being able to go back and do that?”</p>\n<p class=\"p1\"><strong>Laing:</strong> And there’s nothing better than surprising people. When we were able to reflect on it, when we we were shut down, it’s like, there’s nothing better than dropping in on something and not beating somebody over the head. It’s so compelling. “I want in. I want to know what this is, and I’m going to stay.”</p>\n<p class=\"p1\"><strong>Nutting:</strong> We were really pleased the way it fit thematically, too. Because one of the things that the show is really considering is kind of how do you escape from a relationship? And in some ways, is that even possible given memory, given feelings, given the process of grief? Does a marriage end the moment you decide to get divorced? Does it end in a courtroom? Does it end when you’re finally able to move on? All of these questions are coming into play, so we also just loved the idea of this immediacy of escape in a show that is consistently asking, “Will she be able to escape?”</p>\n<p class=\"p1\"><b>When I posted my review, a number of people messaged me saying, “You should read the book, too – it’s wonderful.” I’ve made the tough choice to wait until the show is over to read the book. With that said, having not read the source material myself yet, was it tough to edit your own work and beat it into shape having a team around you? What was the process of reshaping this?</b></p>\n<p class=\"p1\"><strong>Nutting:</strong> The story is essentially about starting over, in both the hope and excitement and, in some ways, impossibility of doing that. So for me it was a very organic process and organic decision to say, “This is a different medium. This is going to demand different things in storytelling.” I want to start over without starting over, taking these characters and themes and spinning something new and unique and wonderful. I was so blessed to have Christina and Stephanie as partners in that storytelling, and was able to create something really special with them.</p>\n<p class=\"p1\"><strong>Lee:</strong> I want to really credit Alissa, because her novel is very internal and she really wanted to expand and adapt from the world, and we talked a lot about what does that mean? It was her decision that she wanted to feel the other perspectives of the characters. In the book, for example, you don’t really know where Byron’s coming from, and in the series, you will.</p>\n<p class=\"p1\"><b>The show is so well-directed. It looks great and the visual comedy is really there. I’m so tired of comedies where they put the camera down and say, “The actors are funny. Let it happen.” There’s such a visual wit in your work in the first episode, Stephanie, that continues into the four episodes that I’ve seen. Can you talk about finding comedy in the filmmaking?</b></p>\n<p class=\"p1\"><strong>Laing:</strong> Absolutely. I mean, listen, collectively, I’m going to say something super cheesy: working with Alissa and Christina, I felt like we had a mind meld. We were all very much in sync from the very beginning, and we’d have the same notes. In between takes, it’d be like, “I’m going to do this,” and [someone else would say], “I was just about to say that!” In terms of bringing it to life visually, we created our own language. We weren’t afraid, and I credit Christina and Alissa in trusting me to do that. We really tried stuff. For me, it was always about the point of view, and I think the best way to film comedy is to not forget that. Whose point of view is this? You can do a cool shot for cool shot’s sake, but there’s no emotion behind it.</p>\n<p class=\"p1\">There’s nothing better than letting something play out, leaving the frame and coming back in and knowing, also, when to move the camera. When not to move the camera. When to sit still and take a breath. It doesn’t happen by accident. It’s very specific. We shot-listed every single thing. We didn’t make up anything on the day. We were very prepared going in, because I know with television your time is so limited. Especially shooting during COVID, we did ten hour days. So we had a plan and we really stuck to it. And then we have tremendous actors. I can’t say enough about how much – we filmed something, but then in a wide, Billy or Cristin would improvise something and it’d be amazing and we would sort of run with that. I would set up a shot around something that they did, which was really rewarding and awesome. I’m so glad that you found it refreshing, because that was the goal.</p>\n<p class=\"p1\"><b>There’s a shot in the first episode where the camera remains at a distance as Cristin Milioti runs toward a car and tries to open the door with beer cans in her hand, and just the camera holds back – the filmmaking itself made me laugh.</b></p>\n<p class=\"p1\"><strong>Laing:</strong> Oh, thank you. I also laughed on the first take of that shot, because it was so clear that there was some subtle physical comedy. She couldn’t get the door open and there was one take where part of the door did come off, because it was a really old truck. I just thought, “We’re going to hang back. We don’t need to be with her. We know she’s getting in the car.” So sometimes it’s just trusting the audience, and again, we don’t need to bang you over the head with this. We’re going to see her in the truck with a person. It’s OK to hang back and see what she does. Physically, Crisitin is so fantastic at that. But how a character runs, how a character walks, all of that goes into the comedy and the performance and the emotion. That particular shot, the choice was just left, like, “I don’t need to be close with her. I need to see her getting into this truck and escaping.” And her struggle with the beer and the sunglasses and the door, it’s human, it’s real. Sometimes, that’s also where comedy comes from: humanity, and the comedy comes from the pain. The reality when you’re trying to escape, and how do you open this when you have a lot of shit in your hand? The beer is important to her in that moment.</p>\n<p class=\"p1\"><b>This show is really funny, but its world feels complete. The science fiction of the series feels like it holds water, and the world of <i>Made for Love</i> feels just shitty enough to be real. Can you talk about balancing the sci-fi world building with the fact that it’s also a relationship comedy?</b></p>\n<p class=\"p1\"><strong>Lee:</strong> We had a lot of those conversations and we played around a lot with that, too. If I told you about some of the silly places that Alissa and I went with the script that we had to pull back on…because our tendencies are toward comedy. What was so great was the team that was around us, some of the people had a comedy background, some of the people had a more dramatic background. So the team that came together, we found this nice balance which was very purposeful. We wanted to tell a sci-fi story that felt different, because we all discussed how we wanted to show a sci-fi story through a female lens. We talked a lot about what does that mean? What have we been missing from sci-fi stories that we’ve seen in the past? That was of the foremost importance, and in that, we wanted heavily to go into the emotional journey of the characters. So that lends itself to be more on the drama side, but I think that the things that make us laugh are all the same. What Stephanie said, the three of us, it’s like we had a chip in our brains. The same weird things would make us laugh, and echoing what Stephanie said, it’s always from a place of realness as opposed to writing a joke. So while you have this dramatic, fantastical scene, the things that are making us laugh are the very human moments that you have. So that tone was found throughout, both in writing and shooting it. And the tone was very easy to find with our actors, who I think approach everything from a very grounded point of view.</p>\n<p class=\"p1\"><strong>Nutting:</strong> I think with tech and sci-fi, so often there’s an emphasis on avoidance or even eradication of emotion and feeling, or even sensation, that it’s all very serious and stripped down. When you think of robots, you don’t think of laughter. Part of us really wanting to imbue this sci-fi story with emotion and warmth, we felt that humor had to stay a critical part of it.</p>\n<p class=\"p1\"><b>I asked my wife what stood out to her in these four episodes, and she said she loved the fact that Hazel is not scared. She is surprised and angry, but she has not spent the entire series so far cowering in fear. That was important to her to see a female lead who was fighting back like that.</b></p>\n<p class=\"p1\"><strong>Lee:</strong> First of all, thank your wife. That’s a very astute observation, and I’m so glad that came across. In a lot of the content that we discuss that we love, that we’re fans of, by the way, we are often following the victim, the one who’s watched, and that person doesn’t have a lot of agency. That’s a key point that we wanted to change, in that we wanted to give her agency. While she is a victim in some ways, she’s finally taking control of her own life and we wanted to see what that looks like. We’ve seen a lot of people running for their lives, but then what happens? That’s the story we wanted to tell.</p>\n<p class=\"p1\"><b>Cristin Milioti is amazing, and may be one of the best actresses working right now. The one-two punch of this and <i>Palm Springs</i> solidifies her as a person where I’m going to see everything she does. Can you talk about building this character for her and how she was cast? She must have been cast when she was on the verge of <i>Palm Springs</i> happening, right?</b></p>\n<p class=\"p1\"><strong>Nutting:</strong> Yeah, it was prior to all of that. She was the only choice. I always joked, “<i>Made for Love</i> was made for Milioti.” She was the only one. I’d seen her dramatic [work] in <i>Fargo</i> and <i>Black Mirror</i>. I knew from her stage work and <i>How I Met Your Mother</i> just how funny she is. There’s really nothing she can’t do. Cristin really helped inform and build this character with us. It was very much a partnership. Her role is so multilayered, and she has to be one character in the Hub, and then she’s another character when she’s out of the Hub. So often, she has to let the viewer know how she’s actually feeling or what she actually thinks is different than what she’s saying aloud or what she’s doing, especially in the Hub. So her attention to nuance and her ability to convey so much with an expression or with her eyes, every episode is such a remarkable performance.</p>\n<p class=\"p1\"><strong>Laing:</strong> I was going to say, for me, when I was directing her, she’s so good, to what Alissa is saying, in the subtleties. I’d be like, “Let’s see a peek of Hub Hazel here with Ray,” and she would just bring it with one look of her eye. “Yep, there she is.” Just finding the levels of performance in everything we did. “Let’s do this take with Hub Hazel and this take with more real world Hazel,” and really fine-tuning that with her – she’s incredible. I can’t imagine there being anyone else in this, other than her.</p>\n<p class=\"p1\"><b>Over the course of the past decade, I’ve enjoyed watching Ray Romano grow from sitcom star into such an interesting actor. Not all people who start out as comedians can do the work he’s been doing over the past ten or fifteen years. Can you talk about bringing him into this and what he brought to the role that wasn’t on the page?</b></p>\n<p class=\"p1\"><strong>Lee:</strong> Yeah, be brought a lot to the role and that character changed because of Ray. The initial characteristics of that father, Herbert, was that he was rough around the edges and he was harder to love and a tougher character to embrace. So it made it really challenging when Hazel came home. But Ray, there’s so much humanity to him, so much vulnerability. You just really love him. Even when he is behaving badly, you feel empathy for him. So he actually changed the way that we wrote that character throughout the series, for the better. I think the character became much more nuanced and believable than sort of a traditional bad dad. You really feel for their relationship and how they’re coming back together in the series, especially in the back end.</p>\n<p class=\"p1\"><b>I want to talk about Billy Magnusson. It’s a really interesting performance. If you jump in a time machine, go back in time 20 years and show people this performance, they’d say, “This guy is an alien. How does he exist?” But somehow, Byron feels like the quintessential villain of 2021 in so many ways. Can you talk about tapping into a very specific type of 21st century bad guy?</b></p>\n<p class=\"p1\"><strong>Lee:</strong> I think Billy also has a lot of humanity, too. I think there’s something in every performance that he’s bringing to it. It’s the same thing that was with Cristin. It was like, “All right, let’s tap into why Byron is who he is.” Alissa alluded to it earlier: we understand a little more about where he’s coming from. So when we get glimpses of that in his performance – although in the first two episodes, you may not know what you’re seeing – it really does pay off later on. That, to me, is how he’s able to become a Byron that we also love, even though he’s terrible.</p>\n<p class=\"p1\"><strong>Laing:</strong> There were times where we’d get notes from the network, and they’d be like, “Wait, are we rooting for them to get back together? I like him!” We were like, “I know!” There are some times where I feel for him.</p>\n<p class=\"p1\"><strong>Nutting:</strong> Yeah, it’s really a credit to his acting and also Billy as a person. The level of empathy that he really brought to this role and to the character, the levels at which he wanted to understand him really helped all of us understand him better. It really shifted the path of the character going forward.</p>\n<p class=\"p1\"><strong>Laing:</strong> Yeah, it really felt like a true collaboration on every level. The three of us basically had a chip implanted in our brains, but then were able to take that and elevate this material with this world that Alissa created. And the details matter, which is why we so appreciate your review, because you noticed that. Every frame mattered. There wasn’t any ounce of us letting go of any small things. Everything mattered.</p>\n<p class=\"p1\"><b>You mentioned the network giving you notes. I’m curious about the relationship between you and HBO Max and how the subject matter of this show is something that we’re finally talking about now. It’s been something that’s been whispered about since as long as human beings have existed, but we’re actively having these conversations about what <i>Made For Love</i> is about out in the open. Was HBO Max like, “Yeah, this is the time, let’s do it”? What were the conversations like to make sure the show could be honest about this stuff?</b></p>\n<p class=\"p1\"><strong>Lee:</strong> I think they were totally game. We had so many conversations with them and among ourselves about what role technology plays in our own lives, especially in this past year. That was sort of interesting, because we were talking about the shortcuts that technology provides in terms of human connection before the pandemic, and then we enter a year in which we’re relying entirely on technology for human connection. We made some changes in our approach to the show while we were shut down, but HBO Max was fully game and they encouraged us to go there. They loved the tech aspect of it. I credit them with saying, “Let’s see even more of that.”</p>\n<p class=\"p1\"><b>Is the plan here that this is just a miniseries, it wraps up the book, and it’s over? Are you leaving any doors open for a season 2, or even an anthology approach where each season is a different story? Have you talked about that at all? </b></p>\n<p class=\"p1\"><strong>Nutting:</strong> We really fell so in love with these characters and the actors playing them, but also the themes and the questions and the conversations, as you mentioned, around technology. There’s so much there, we would absolutely love to do a season 2, yeah.</p>\n<p class=\"p1\"><b>Could all of you share a movie or TV show that you think would pair really well with <i>Made for Love</i> that our readers should watch before or after this?</b></p>\n<p class=\"p1\"><strong>Laing:</strong> This is a funny one, because the content is completely different. But I just started watching <i>Get Shorty</i>, which I hadn’t seen before we shot this even though Ray and Billy are in it. I am dying of laughter and seeing those two also in another show is a pure delight. Different genres, but I’d say if you like the actors in our show and you haven’t seen <i>Get Shorty</i>, go see that show.</p>\n<p class=\"p1\"><strong>Lee:</strong> If you’re looking for a movie and then this, a good one for me would be <i>Marriage Story</i> and then this, for very different reasons.</p>\n<p class=\"p1\"><strong>Nutting:</strong> TV-wise, I think <i>Devs</i> is a cool companion, looking at some of the similar tech questions and themes in different subjects outside of romantic relationships.</p>\n<p>The post <a rel=\"nofollow\" /></p>\n<p><strong>Director Eli Roth&#8217;s<em> Borderlands</em></strong> is looking to be the most star-studded video game adaptation yet. With cast members like <strong>Cate Blanchett</strong> and <strong>Jack Black</strong> on the call sheet, it&#8217;s immediately one of the more interesting feature film adaptations of a popular video game to come along in years. So all eyes are on the <em>Borderlands</em> production, which has just started filming in Hungary.</p>\n<p><span id=\"more-665240\"></span></p>\n<p><strong>Ariana Greenblatt</strong>, who played Young Gamora in <em>Avengers: Infinity War</em> and is set to play a character named Tiny Tina in Eli Roth&#8217;s <em>Borderlands</em> movie, revealed that cameras are rolling on the production of the video game adaptation in a Thursday tweet that included a photo with her and Roth.</p>\n<blockquote class=\"twitter-tweet\" data-width=\"550\" data-dnt=\"true\">\n<p lang=\"en\" dir=\"ltr\">we out here, cameras rolling?  Day1??? <a href=\"https://twitter.com/hashtag/BorderlandsMovie?src=hash&#38;ref_src=twsrc%5Etfw\">#BorderlandsMovie</a> <a href=\"https://t.co/PASJ9rw2Eb\">pic.twitter.com/PASJ9rw2Eb</a></p>\n<p>&#8212; Ariana Greenblatt (@ArianaG) <a href=\"https://twitter.com/ArianaG/status/1377677890783911936?ref_src=twsrc%5Etfw\">April 1, 2021</a></p></blockquote>\n<p><script async src=\"https://platform.twitter.com/widgets.js\" charset=\"utf-8\"></script></p>\n<p>Eli Roth is directing the <em>Borderlands</em> movie from a script by <em>Chernobyl</em> creator <strong>Craig Mazin</strong>, based on the popular Gearbox Software video game franchise.</p>\n<p>The original <em>Borderlands</em> game from 2009 followed a band of &#8220;Vault Hunters&#8221; looking for an alien vault on the planet of Pandora. Set in the distant future, when mega-corporations vie for control of planets to colonize and mine for their natural resources, the Vault Hunters battle the local wildlife and bandit population as they fight to stop the leader of a private corporation army from reaching the alien vault before they do. The game spawned three sequels: <i>Borderlands 2</i> in 2012, <i>Borderlands: The Pre-Sequel</i> in 2014, and <em>Borderlands 3</em> in 2019.<span id=\"more-660133\"></span></p>\n<p>In Roth&#8217;s <em>Borderlands</em>, <strong>Cate Blanchett</strong> <a href=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/borderlands-movie-cast/\">will play</a> a super-powered woman named Lilith, <strong>Kevin Hart</strong> <a href=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/kevin-hart-borderlands/\">will play</a> a stoic soldier named Roland, <strong>Jamie Lee Curtis</strong> <a href=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/borderlands-movie-cast-adds-halloween-and-knives-out-star-jamie-lee-curtis/\">is playing</a> an archeologist named Tannis, and <strong>Jack Black</strong> <a href=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/borderlands-movie-cast-jack-black/\">is playing</a> a sarcastic robot named Claptrap. Haley Bennett and Florian Munteanu have also joined the film.</p>\n<p>Stay tuned as <em>Borderlands</em> continues production, likely for the next few months amid COVID-19 restrictions. There is no set release date from Lionsgate yet.</p>\n<p>The post <a rel=\"nofollow\" href=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/eli-roth-borderlands-movie-filming/\">Eli Roth&#8217;s &#8216;Borderlands&#8217; Sideshow and Hot Toys is pleased to present the Batman Sixth Scale Collectible Figure from <em>Batman Begins</em> as an exclusive item, available only in selected markets!</p>\n<p>The highly-detailed figure is skillfully crafted based on the screen appearance of Batman in the movie, featuring a head sculpt of Christian Bale as Bruce Wayne with amazing likeness; a masked head sculpt with 3 interchangeable lower faces of different expressions; newly developed specialized body; finely tailored Batsuit and cape attached; detail recreations of Batman’s signature gadgets and weapons including Batarangs, a bomb, climbing harness, balaclava, communicator and a figure base.</p></blockquote>\n\n<a href='https://www.slashfilm.com/hot-toys-batman-begins-figure-and-batmobile/batmanbegins-hottoys-batman-photo2/'><img width=\"346\" height=\"500\" src=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/batmanbegins-hottoys-batman-photo2-346x500.jpg\" class=\"attachment-thumbnail size-thumbnail\" alt=\"Hot Toys Batman Begins - Batman Figure\" srcset=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/batmanbegins-hottoys-batman-photo2-346x500.jpg 346w, https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/batmanbegins-hottoys-batman-photo2.jpg 700w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 346px) 100vw, 346px\" /></a>\n<a href='https://www.slashfilm.com/hot-toys-batman-begins-figure-and-batmobile/batmanbegins-hottoys-batman-photo5/'><img width=\"346\" height=\"500\" src=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/batmanbegins-hottoys-batman-photo5-346x500.jpg\" class=\"attachment-thumbnail size-thumbnail\" alt=\"Hot Toys Batman Begins - Batman Figure\" srcset=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/batmanbegins-hottoys-batman-photo5-346x500.jpg 346w, https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/batmanbegins-hottoys-batman-photo5.jpg 700w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 346px) 100vw, 346px\" /></a>\n\n<p>Along with a totally unmasked face of Bruce Wayne, it&#8217;s nice to see that the growling mouth of Christian Bale has a few interchangeable expressions. Watching Bale&#8217;s face is almost as fascinating as listening to his growl when he puts on the cape and cowl.</p>\n<p>You can pre-order the Hot Toys <em>Batman Begins</em> <a href=\"https://www.sideshow.com/collectibles/dc-comics-batman-hot-toys-908079\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">right now for $255</a>, and it will arrive in the third quarter of <strong>2022</strong>.</p>\n<p><img class=\"size-medium wp-image-665161 aligncenter\" src=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/batmanbegins-hottoys-batmobile-photo1-700x490.jpg\" alt=\"Hot Toys Batman Begins Batmobile\" width=\"700\" height=\"490\" srcset=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/batmanbegins-hottoys-batmobile-photo1.jpg 700w, https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/batmanbegins-hottoys-batmobile-photo1-360x252.jpg 360w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 700px) 100vw, 700px\" /></p>\n<h2>Hot Toys Batman Begins Batmobile</h2>\n<blockquote><p>Based on Christopher Nolan’s The Dark Knight trilogy, Sideshow and Hot Toys present the super-vehicle Batmobile as a stunning sixth scale collectible vehicle that can be paired with Batman figure to recreate more breathtaking scenes!</p>\n<p>The highly-detailed collectible has captured Batmobile’s appearance in the movie with extreme precision and outstanding painting applications, complemented with perfectly scaled design and mechanical details throughout its interior and body. Measuring at approximately 73cm in length, it features LED light-up functions throughout the vehicle body; rotatable rubber tires; also more exquisite mechanical features such as slide-open roof panel, and articulated breaking flaps.</p></blockquote>\n<p><img class=\"size-medium wp-image-665159 aligncenter\" 12:49:03","updatedTime":"2021-04-03 12:49:03","title":"Sam Raimi-Produced Horror Movie ‘Every House is Haunted’ Lands at Netflix","link":"https://www.slashfilm.com/?p=665184","description":"<p><img class=\"aligncenter size-medium wp-image-665187\" src=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/every-house-is-haunted-e1617370231448-700x299.jpeg\" alt=\"every house is haunted movie\" https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/every-house-is-haunted-e1617370231448-360x154.jpeg 360w, https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/every-house-is-haunted-e1617370231448-768x328.jpeg 768w, https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/every-house-is-haunted-e1617370231448.jpeg 1024w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 700px) 100vw, 700px\" /></p>\n<p><strong><em>Every House is Haunted</em></strong>, especially for Netflix. The streamer, which knows a thing or two about <a href=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/haunting-of-bly-manor-spoiler-review/\">haunted houses</a>, has landed the <strong>Sam Raimi</strong>-produced horror movie <em>Every House is Haunted</em>, based on Ian Rogers&#8217; collection of supernatural short stories.</p>\n<p><span id=\"more-665184\"></span></p>\n<p>Deadline reports that the <em>Every House is Haunted</em> movie will be coming to Netflix. Written by <strong>Jason Pagan</strong> and <strong>Andrew Deutschman</strong>, <em>Every House is Haunted </em>will be directed by <strong>Corin Hardy</strong>, best known for helming <em>The Nun</em> and episodes of <em>Gangs of London</em>. Raimi will be producing the movie alongside Zainab Azizi for Raimi Productions, with Roy Lee for Vertigo Entertainment and Vertigo’s Andrew Childs executive producing.</p>\n<p>In <em>Every House is Haunted</em>, &#8220;An insurance investigator tries to debunk claims that a couple’s death was caused by a haunted house, but his doubts are challenged by a psychic and the mysterious occurrences he witnesses with his own eyes.&#8221;</p>\n<p>The feature film is based on Ian Rogers&#8217; collection of short stories published in 2012. Here is the synopsis for the <em>Every House is Haunted</em> short story collection (via <a href=\"https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/15904026-every-house-is-haunted\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">GoodReads</a>):</p>\n<blockquote><p>In this brilliant debut collection, Ian Rogers explores the border-places between our world and the dark reaches of the supernatural. The landscape of death becomes the new frontier for scientific exploration. With remarkable deftness, Rogers draws together the disturbing and the diverting in twenty-two showcase stories that will guide you through terrain at once familiar and startlingly fresh.</p></blockquote>\n<p>The film, however, won&#8217;t be an anthology of all the stories, but based primarily on the short story &#8220;The House on Ashley Avenue<em>.&#8221;</em> The story follows a pair of paranormal investigators who try to find out why the house on Ashley Avenue isn&#8217;t on the real estate market, with the film taking a few liberties with the premise (one insurance investigator versus two, a mysterious murder, etc.).</p>\n<p>But it seems like <em>Every House is Haunted</em> is in good hands, with a big horror name like Raimi producing — through the filmmaker&#8217;s financing deal with Starlight, which optioned the short story collection — and Hardy directing after taking on the<em> Conjuring</em> spin-off film <em>The Nun</em>. And of course, it&#8217;s got a welcome home at Netflix, which has found major success with haunted house titles, and the horror market in general, particularly with Mike Flanagan&#8217;s <em>Haunting of Hill House</em> anthology series. Per Deadline, Netflix came in with the strongest bid for <em>Every House is Haunted</em> after the project was shopped around Hollywood.</p>\n<p>No cast or release date has yet been set for <em>Every House is Haunted</em>.</p>\n<p>The post <a rel=\"nofollow\" href=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/every-house-is-haunted-movie-netflix/\">Sam Raimi-Produced Horror Movie &#8216;Every House is 360w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 700px) 100vw, 700px\" /></p>\n<p>In HBO&#8217;s hit series <em>Game of Thrones</em>, <strong>Emilia Clarke</strong> was one of the most powerful would-be rulers of Westeros. But in the new true crime thriller <strong><em>Above Suspicion</em></strong>, she&#8217;s just a desperate woman trying to escape a dead end coal-mining town in Kentucky any way she can.</p>\n<p>Susan Smith (Clarke) thinks her big ticket out of town has arrived when FBI agent Mark Putnam (<strong>Jack Huston</strong>) uses her as an informant, even going so far as to strike up an intimate relationship with her while the case unfolds. But when the job is done, he skips town and goes back to his wife and kids, leaving Susan high and dry. And that&#8217;s just not something she&#8217;s going to tolerate. Listen to Emilia Clarke&#8217;s Southern accent and see how far she&#8217;s willing to go in the <em>Above Suspicion</em> trailer below.<span id=\"more-665193\"></span></p>\n<h2>Above Suspicion Trailer</h2>\n<p><iframe width=\"740\" height=\"416\" src=\"https://www.youtube.com/embed/lJnmaDLRx5k?feature=oembed\" frameborder=\"0\" allow=\"accelerometer; autoplay; clipboard-write; encrypted-media; gyroscope; picture-in-picture\" allowfullscreen></iframe></p>\n<p>If the premise itself didn&#8217;t already sound worthy of an episode of <em>Jerry Springer</em>, there&#8217;s also the added twist of Susan Smith being pregnant, which makes the FBI agent even more of a scumbag. Meanwhile, <strong>Johnny Knoxville</strong> is also kicking around as a seemingly scorned former lover who doesn&#8217;t want anything to do with Susan now that she&#8217;s been kicked to the curb. It all feels like a gritty Lifetime movie, and not even the fact that it&#8217;s based on a true story is doing the material any favors.</p>\n<p>The only hope that this movie might turn out better than it seems is that it&#8217;s directed by <strong>Phillip Noyce</strong>, who previously directed <em>The Bone Collector</em>, <em>Patriot Games</em>, and <em>Clear and Present Danger</em>. At the same time, the last major movie he helmed was the underwhelming adaptation of <em>The Giver</em>, so he seems to have lost his touch in recent years.</p>\n<p>The rest of the cast includes <strong>Sophie Lowe</strong>, <strong>Austin Hébert</strong>, <strong>Karl Glusman</strong>, <strong>Chris Mulkey</strong>, <strong>Omar Miller</strong>, <strong>Kevin Dunn</strong> and <strong>Thora Birch</strong>. But it&#8217;s probably not going to be the kind of movie they&#8217;re happy to see in parentheses next to their name.</p>\n<blockquote><p>Based on the true story of one of the most notorious crimes in FBI history, this gritty crime-thriller stars Emilia Clarke (“Game of Thrones”) as Susan Smith, a young woman desperate to escape a seedy life of crime and drugs in a Kentucky coal mining town. When a newly minted FBI agent named Mark Putnam (Jack Huston, “Fargo”) recruits Susan as his informant for a high-profile case, she believes her bad luck may finally be changing. But as Susan and Putnam’s relationship deepens, so does the danger, setting them both on a collision course with deadly consequences.</p></blockquote>\n<p><em>Above Suspicion</em> arrives in select theaters and on VOD starting on <strong><em>May 14, 2021</em></strong>.</p>\n<p>The post <a rel=\"nofollow\" Anime","link":"https://www.slashfilm.com/?p=665207","description":"<p><img class=\"aligncenter size-medium wp-image-665214\" src=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/yasuke-700x349.jpg\" https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/yasuke-768x383.jpg 768w, https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/yasuke.jpg 1440w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 700px) 100vw, 700px\" /></p>\n<p>In 16th century Japan, an African slave became the first-ever Black man to step into the country, piquing the interest of Japanese warlord Oda Nobunaga. He eventually gained the trust, friendship, and respect of Nobunaga, and would ascend to the title of samurai, becoming known as the legendary Black samurai, Yasuke. But while Yasuke existed in our world, the demons he&#8217;s fighting in the new Netflix anime series <strong><em>Yasuke</em></strong>, probably weren&#8217;t. Inspired by the legend of the Black samurai, <em>Yasuke</em> stars <strong>LaKeith Stanfield</strong> as the titular character, who is brought back into battle to raise an army against an unspeakable evil. Watch the <em>Y</em><em>asuke </em>trailer below.</p>\n<p><span id=\"more-665207\"></span></p>\n<h2>Yasuke Trailer</h2>\n<p><iframe width=\"740\" height=\"416\" src=\"https://www.youtube.com/embed/oYcK1LQl_Fs?feature=oembed\" frameborder=\"0\" allow=\"accelerometer; autoplay; clipboard-write; encrypted-media; gyroscope; picture-in-picture\" allowfullscreen></iframe></p>\n<p><i>Yasuke</i> is created by <strong>LeSean Thomas</strong> (<i>Cannon Busters</i>) who also serves as executive producer and director, and comes from the acclaimed Japanese animation studio MAPPA, which is behind hits such as <em>Attack on Titan</em> and <i>Jujutsu Kaisen</i><em>.</em> And it stars none other than Oscar nominee LaKeith Stanfield, who voices Yasuke and also executive produces the alternate-history series inspired by the legendary real-life Black samurai. Only this time, he&#8217;s fighting mechs and magic.</p>\n<p>The trailer promises a gory, action-packed anime series, with impressive character design by director and animator <strong>Takeshi Koike</strong> (<i>Lupin the Third: The Woman Called Fujiko Mine</i>) and music by Grammy-nominated artist Flying Lotus. But I do have to say that Stanfield&#8217;s very recognizable timbre is a tad distracting. There&#8217;s an ongoing conversation about casting <a href=\"https://www.theatlantic.com/entertainment/archive/2011/10/how-celebrities-took-over-cartoon-voice-acting/247481/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">celebrities in voice acting roles</a>, and while Stanfield is a talented actor, I&#8217;m still not convinced he will deliver as a voice actor, which requires a very different acting muscle than screen acting.</p>\n<p>Still, <em>Yasuke</em> has an impressive creative team behind it, with MAPPA and Koike lending credibility to the Netflix anime, which is more than you could say for the streamer&#8217;s <a href=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/pacific-rim-the-black-spoiler-review/\">many other attempts</a> to corner the anime market. And since we&#8217;re likely not going to get the live-action <a href=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/yasuke-cast-chadwick-boseman/\">feature film about Yasuke</a>, which originally was set to star the lateChadwick Boseman, this is a more than worthy alternative.</p>\n<p>Here is the synopsis to <em>Yasuke</em>:</p>\n<blockquote><p>The tale is set in a war-torn feudal Japan filled with mechs and magic, the greatest ronin never known, <i>Yasuke</i>, struggles to maintain a peaceful existence after a past life of violence. But when a local village becomes the center of social upheaval between warring daimyo, <i>Yasuke</i> must take up his sword and transport a mysterious child who is the target of dark forces and bloodthirsty warlords. <u></u><u></u></p></blockquote>\n<p><em>Yasuke</em> is set to debut on Netflix on <strong>April 29, 2021</strong>. 100vw, 700px\" /></p>\n<p>The last couple years have seen the introduction of new streaming competitors like HBO Max, Peacock and Paramount+, and the streaming wars are heating up as each of them try to create a library of movies and TV shows that will entice viewers to subscribe. Each of those new services fall under parent companies who also own movie studios, but only one of them hasn&#8217;t yet taken full advantage of that relationship.</p>\n<p>Even though Peacock falls under the Comcast banner that includes Universal Pictures, the NBCUniversal streaming service isn&#8217;t exclusively streaming any of the movie studio&#8217;s major franchises like <strong><em>Fast and Furious</em></strong> or <strong><em>Jurassic Park</em></strong>. But it sounds like that could change in the near future as NBCUniversal is considering the possibility of making Universal Pictures movies exclusive to Peacock.<span id=\"more-665218\"></span></p>\n<p><a href=\"https://www.bloomberg.com/news/articles/2021-03-31/comcast-weighs-pulling-universal-s-movies-from-hbo-max-netflix\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">Bloomberg</a> has news that NBCUniversal is currently trying to figure out if they want to end licensing deals with the likes of HBO Max and Netflix in order to build the library of movies that are exclusive to Peacock. Right now, HBO Max has a deal that gives them the rights to play Universal Pictures movies nine months after they leave theaters. Meanwhile, Netflix does the same thing with Universal&#8217;s animation studio Illumination Entertainment, which includes the <strong><em>Despicable Me</em></strong> and <strong><em>Secret Life of Pets</em></strong> franchises. Both of these deals are up at the end of the year.</p>\n<p>A decision hasn&#8217;t been made by NBCUniversal yet simply because they&#8217;re trying to figure out if it&#8217;s more beneficial to make these movies exclusive to Peacock in order to boost their subscription numbers. If franchises like <em>Fast and the Furious</em>, <em>Jurassic Park</em> and <del>the Dark Universe</del> the Jason Bourne series become exclusive to Peacock, then Universal doesn&#8217;t make as much money from selling the licensing rights to other streamers. But there is the possibility of seeing a hybrid approach to these streaming deals.</p>\n<p>Last year, Universal was already leaning towards striking new deals to license movies to other streaming services. But the coronavirus pandemic apparently put a hold on those negotiations, hence the potential move to Peacock. One possible outcome could see Peacock sharing the streaming rights to Universal Pictures movies with one of the other streaming services. For example, Peacock shares the streaming rights to the hit series <em>Modern Family</em> with Hulu. Doing the same with some of Universal&#8217;s movies would be a way for NBCUniversal and Universal Pictures to have the best of both worlds.</p>\n<p>As of now, Peacock is probably on the lower end of the streaming wars right now. Their library of exclusive titles isn&#8217;t all that impressive, which is why the price of the subscription tiers is directly linked to how much of <em>The Office</em> you want to be able to watch. But Peacock is in the midst of building a library of original shows, including the the reboot of <em>Saved by the Bell</em>, the upcoming comedy <a href=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/rutherford-falls-trailer/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\"><em>Rutherford Falls</em></a>, a new series <a href=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/poker-face-rian-johnson/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">from <em>Knives Out</em> director Rian Johnson</a>, an adaptation of <a href=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/wild-cards-tv-series-moves-to-peacock/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">George R.R. Martin&#8217;s <em>Wild Cards</em></a>, and <a href=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/category/distributors/television-distributors/peacock/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">much more</a>.</p>\n<p>It&#8217;s not clear when a decision on Universal&#8217;s streaming plans will be made, but we&#8217;ll keep you posted.</p>\n<p>The post <a rel=\"nofollow\" href=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/universal-movies-streaming-on-peacock/\">Peacock May Become the Exclusive Streaming Home to Universal Franchises Like &#8216;Fast and Furious&#8217; and &#8216;Jurassic Park&#8217;</a> appeared first on <a rel=\"nofollow\" href=\"https://www.slashfilm.com\">/Film</a>.</p>\n<div class=\"feedflare\">\n<a of Netflix&#8217;s biggest hits when it debuted its first season back in December 2019. The fantasy adventure series, full of <strong>Henry Cavill</strong>&#8216;s rippling muscles ripping up terrifying monsters, felt like it was destined to be a hit, as it was based on the beloved video games and the novels by Polish writer Andrzej Sapkowski. And as <em>The Witcher</em> season 2 finally wraps, overcoming a COVID-restricted production, showrunner <strong>Lauren Schmidt Hissrich</strong> teases more storylines from Sapkowski&#8217;s novels to come.</p>\n<p><span id=\"more-665229\"></span></p>\n<p><iframe width=\"740\" height=\"416\" src=\"https://www.youtube.com/embed/3cKSG5lkhto?start=1&#038;feature=oembed\" frameborder=\"0\" allow=\"accelerometer; autoplay; clipboard-write; encrypted-media; gyroscope; picture-in-picture\" allowfullscreen></iframe></p>\n<p>That&#8217;s a wrap for <em>The Witcher</em> Season 2, which finished its 158-day production over the course of the coronavirus (COVID-19) pandemic. The celebratory video for <em>The Witcher</em> season 2 filming wrap reveals that the production took extra precautions amid the pandemic, and still managed to finish shooting in 15 locations with 89 cast members and over 1200 different crew members. The behind-the-scenes video also came accompanied by a tweet featuring Cavill with a clapper board.</p>\n<blockquote class=\"twitter-tweet\" data-width=\"550\" data-dnt=\"true\">\n<p lang=\"en\" dir=\"ltr\">That&#39;s a wrap on Season 2! The White Wolf awaits you back on The Continent. <a href=\"https://t.co/SqrAbeelob\">pic.twitter.com/SqrAbeelob</a></p>\n<p>&#8212; The Witcher (@witchernetflix) <a href=\"https://twitter.com/witchernetflix/status/1377969128502403077?ref_src=twsrc%5Etfw\">April 2, 2021</a></p></blockquote>\n<p><script async src=\"https://platform.twitter.com/widgets.js\" charset=\"utf-8\"></script></p>\n<p>&#8220;We&#8217;re so proud of everything we&#8217;ve accomplished in Season 2 and we can&#8217;t wait for you to watch it,&#8221; Hissrich said in the video, which showed behind-the-scenes glimpses of the second season, as well as teased the season&#8217;s storylines. &#8220;We cannot wait to show you what Geralt, and Ciri, and Yennefer, and Jaskier, and all of your favorites have been up to since we left them at the Battle of Sodden Hill. There are plenty of new characters and storylines, and of course, monsters, to explore as well, as we dig into the <em>Blood of Elves</em> and beyond,&#8221; Hissrich teased.</p>\n<p>Published in 1994, <em>Blood of Elves</em> is the third novel in <em>the Witcher</em> saga written by Andrzej Sapkowski. It is a sequel to <em>the Witcher</em> short story collections <em>Sword of Destiny</em> and <em>The Last Wish</em>, and follows Geralt as he takes the exiled princess Ciri under his wing.</p>\n<p data-pw-in-article=\"true\">Cavill (<em>Mission Impossible – Fallout, Man of Steel</em>) returns in <em>The Witcher </em>as Geralt of Rivia, alongside<strong> Anya Chalotra</strong> as Yennefer and <strong>Freya Allan </strong>as Ciri, and <strong>Joey Batey</strong> as everyone’s favorite bard Jaskier.</p>\n<p data-pw-in-article=\"true\">In addition to returning cast members, the show is bringing a host of new faces to face off against Geralt of Rivia in <em>The Witcher</em> season 2. The cast for season 2 includes <em>Game of Thrones</em> alum <strong>Kristofer Hivju </strong>as Nivellen, <strong>Yasen Atour</strong> (<em>Young Wallender</em>) as Coen, <strong>Agnes Bjorn</strong> as Vereena, <strong>Paul Bullion</strong> (<em>Peaky Blinders)</em> as Lambert, <strong>Thue Ersted Rasmussen</strong> (<em>Fast and Furious 9</em>) as Eskel, <strong>Aisha Fabienne Ross</strong> (<em>The Danish Girl</em>) as Lydia, and recent graduate <strong>Mecia Simson</strong> as Francesca.</p>\n<p data-pw-in-article=\"true\"><em>The Witcher </em>Season 2 is expected to premiere on Netflix sometime in 2021.</p>\n<p>The post <a rel=\"nofollow\" href=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/chucky-tv-series-production.jpg\"><img class=\"aligncenter size-medium wp-image-665255\" 700px) 100vw, 700px\" /></a></p>\n<p>At long last, the <strong><em>Chucky</em> </strong>TV series has begun filming. The <em>Child&#8217;s Play</em> spin-off series was supposed to start shooting last year but COVID-19 got in the way. Now, <em>Chucky</em> co-creator <strong>Don Mancini</strong> has revealed that the SYFY series is finally in production – and that we&#8217;ll likely get to see it this fall. The series follows a suburban town plunged into chaos when a Good Guy doll turns up at a yard sale. <strong>Devon Sawa</strong> is part of the cast, as is original Chucky voice actor <strong>Brad Dourif</strong>. And on the heels production kicking off, <em>Arrow</em>&#8216;s <strong>Lexa Doig</strong> has joined the cast as well.</p>\n<p><span id=\"more-665237\"></span></p>\n<p>Don Mancini broke the news that the <em>Chucky</em> TV series production had begun, stating on <a href=\"https://twitter.com/RealDonMancini/status/1377635961115443207?ref_src=twsrc%5Etfw%7Ctwcamp%5Etweetembed%7Ctwterm%5E1377635961115443207%7Ctwgr%5E%7Ctwcon%5Es1_&#38;ref_url=https%3A%2F%2Fcollider.com%2Fchucky-series-childs-play-series-premiere-date%2F\">social media</a> that &#8220;the series is officially in production and coming to USA Network and SYFY this fall.&#8221; Cast member Devon Sawa confirmed this as well:</p>\n<blockquote class=\"twitter-tweet\" data-width=\"550\" data-dnt=\"true\">\n<p lang=\"en\" dir=\"ltr\">Day one for me on this show with the little fella. <a href=\"https://t.co/Tsk4PzCIE6\">pic.twitter.com/Tsk4PzCIE6</a></p>\n<p>&#8212; devon sawa (@DevonESawa) <a href=\"https://twitter.com/DevonESawa/status/1377572159187472387?ref_src=twsrc%5Etfw\">April 1, 2021</a></p></blockquote>\n<p><script async src=\"https://platform.twitter.com/widgets.js\" charset=\"utf-8\"></script></p>\n<p>A continuation of the <em>Child&#8217;s Play</em> series, <em>Chucky</em> kicks off when a &#8220;vintage Chucky doll turns up at a suburban yard sale.&#8221; The result: &#8220;An idyllic American town is thrown into chaos as a series of horrifying murders begin to expose the town’s hypocrisies and secrets. Meanwhile, the arrival of enemies — and allies — from Chucky’s past threatens to expose the truth behind the killings, as well as the demon doll’s untold origins as a seemingly ordinary child who somehow became this notorious monster.&#8221;</p>\n<p>In addition to Sawa, the series brings back Brad Dourif as the voice of Chucky. Dourif&#8217;s daughter <strong>Fiona Dourif</strong>, who appeared in the previous two <em>Chucky</em> movies, is on board as well, as is franchise player<strong> Jennifer Tilly</strong>. New additions to the franchise include <strong>Zackary Arthur</strong> (<em>Transparent</em>), <strong>Teo Briones</strong> (<em>Ratched</em>), <strong>Bjorgvin Arnarson</strong> (<em>PEN15</em>), and <strong>Alyvia Alyn Lind</strong> (<em>The Young and the Restless</em>). And <a href=\"https://www.syfy.com/syfywire/lexa-doig-cast-in-chucky-tv-series-syfy-usa?__source=soc_twitter_x_x_SYFYWIRE_org_link_SYFYWIRE_x_wire_x_x&#38;utm_source=twitter&#38;utm_medium=social&#38;utm_campaign=x_x_SYFYWIRE_org_link_SYFYWIRE_x_wire_x&#38;utm_term=organic&#38;utm_content=link_ad\">SYFY</a> reports that Lexa Doig has joined the cast as well, playing Bree Webber. She&#8217;s married to Logan (played by Sawa), and the aunt of Jake Webber (Arthur). She&#8217;s also &#8220;held to an unrealistic standard — by her husband and herself, which leads her to keep a dark secret from her family.&#8221;</p>\n<p><em>Chucky</em> is firmly rooted within the main <em>Child&#8217;s Play</em>/<em>Chucky</em> franchise, which is still going strong. In 2019 there was a <em>Child&#8217;s Play</em> reboot, but that film is completely unconnected from the primary series. Don Mancini, the co-creator of the franchise, has remained a constant presence throughout the entire series, and he&#8217;s on board to write and direct episodes of the TV series as well.</p>\n<p>The class=\"aligncenter size-medium wp-image-665268\" src=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/justice-league-we-live-in-a-society-scene-700x321.jpg\" alt=\"justice league we live in a society 948w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 700px) 100vw, 700px\" /></a></p>\n<p>Before <strong><em>Zack Snyder&#8217;s Justice League</em> </strong>arrived on HBO Max a trailer dropped featuring <strong>Jared Leto</strong>&#8216;s Joker saying, &#8220;We live in a society!&#8221; It was painfully stupid, and it was clearly meant to &#8220;break the internet&#8221; and drum up more hype, since the Joker saying &#8220;We live in a society&#8221; has become a long-running <a href=\"https://happymag.tv/we-live-in-a-society-meme-explained/\">meme</a> on the internet. Curiously enough, the line didn&#8217;t actually end up in the film itself. Now, <strong>Zack Snyder</strong> has gone ahead and uploaded it online and you can watch it below, if you&#8217;re so inclined.</p>\n<p><span id=\"more-665259\"></span></p>\n<h2><strong>We Live In A Society</strong></h2>\n<blockquote class=\"twitter-tweet\" data-width=\"550\" data-dnt=\"true\">\n<p lang=\"en\" dir=\"ltr\">We live in a society&#8230; where you can watch <a href=\"https://twitter.com/hashtag/ZackSnydersJusticeLeague?src=hash&#38;ref_src=twsrc%5Etfw\">#ZackSnydersJusticeLeague</a> on <a href=\"https://twitter.com/hbomax?ref_src=twsrc%5Etfw\">@HBOMax</a>. <a href=\"https://t.co/8l3CwvynZq\">https://t.co/8l3CwvynZq</a>  <a href=\"https://twitter.com/hashtag/SnyderCut?src=hash&#38;ref_src=twsrc%5Etfw\">#SnyderCut</a> <a href=\"https://twitter.com/hashtag/UsUnited?src=hash&#38;ref_src=twsrc%5Etfw\">#UsUnited</a> <a href=\"https://twitter.com/hashtag/AFSP?src=hash&#38;ref_src=twsrc%5Etfw\">#AFSP</a> <a href=\"https://twitter.com/hashtag/weliveinasociety?src=hash&#38;ref_src=twsrc%5Etfw\">#weliveinasociety</a> <a href=\"https://t.co/V8pmWFnVIf\">pic.twitter.com/V8pmWFnVIf</a></p>\n<p>&#8212; Zack Snyder (@ZackSnyder) <a href=\"https://twitter.com/ZackSnyder/status/1378007017202229249?ref_src=twsrc%5Etfw\">April 2, 2021</a></p></blockquote>\n<p><script async src=\"https://platform.twitter.com/widgets.js\" charset=\"utf-8\"></script></p>\n<p>I liked <em>Zack Snyder&#8217;s Justice League</em>. I have some problems with it (which you can read all about <a href=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/zack-snyders-justice-league-review/\">here</a>), but overall, the film is a fascinating experiment and I&#8217;m glad it exists. That said, there&#8217;s one scene in the film that&#8217;s absolutely awful and should&#8217;ve remained cut – the so-called Knightmare sequence, where <strong>Ben Affleck</strong>&#8216;s Batman/Bruce Wayne has a bad dream about an alternate future where Superman is evil and the intergalactic villain Darkseid has taken over the world. It&#8217;s a painfully dull, needless bleak epilogue that ruins a perfectly acceptable, upbeat ending. Making matters worse is a downright craptacular scene between Batman and the Joker, played by Jared Leto. Leto hams it up to the extreme, delivering an edgelord monologue that goes on, and on, and on.</p>\n<p>But believe it or not, as long as this scene is, it could&#8217;ve been even longer! Director Zack Snyder took to social media to upload a longer, uncut version of the scene, and it&#8217;s here where we get to witness Leto say, &#8220;We live in a society!&#8221; Snyder splices the deleted sequence into the officially released scene, which results in a moment where we get to see Affleck and Leto standing in front of a green screen (the actors filmed their moments separately and Snyder cut them together).</p>\n<p>Does adding this back in make the scene better? Absolutely not – it&#8217;s still just as lousy as it was to begin with. But fans who are hungering for more will no doubt be happy to have this, and isn&#8217;t that what living in a society is all about?</p>\n<p>The post <a rel=\"nofollow\" href=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/justice-league-we-live-in-a-society-scene/\">You Can Now Watch the Deleted &#8220;We Live In a Society&#8221; Joker Scene From &#8216;Zack Snyder&#8217;s Justice League&#8217;</a> appeared first on <a rel=\"nofollow\" href=\"https://www.slashfilm.com\">/Film</a>.</p>\n<div class=\"feedflare\">\n<a subscribed to the Disney streaming service. But after a month of being available only in theaters and in Premier Access, <em>Raya and the Last Dragon</em> is coming to home video. The Disney fantasy epic releases to Digital today, and /Film is debuting an exclusive deleted scene from its bonus features. Watch the <em>Raya and the Last Dragon</em> deleted scene below.</p>\n<p><span id=\"more-665179\"></span></p>\n<h2>Raya and the Last Dragon Deleted Scene</h2>\n<p><iframe width=\"740\" height=\"416\" src=\"https://www.youtube.com/embed/31EyApWJxLE?feature=oembed\" frameborder=\"0\" allow=\"accelerometer; autoplay; clipboard-write; encrypted-media; gyroscope; picture-in-picture\" allowfullscreen></iframe></p>\n<p>Did you know that Raya&#8217;s sword used to be a magic sword? We didn&#8217;t either, but that was apparently a real important element of <em>Raya and the Last Dragon</em> before it got cut (pun not intended). But this <em>Raya and the Last Dragon</em> deleted scene, which is shown in storyboard form with voice acting and sound effects included, gives us a glimpse at an early chapter in the story when Raya&#8217;s sword used to have magic powers that could slay the evil Druun.</p>\n<p>In <em>Raya and the Last Dragon</em>, &#8220;it’s up to a lone warrior, Raya, to track down the last dragon in order to finally stop the Druun for good. However, along her journey, she’ll learn that it’ll take more than dragon magic to save the world—it’s going to take trust as well.&#8221; Kelly Marie Tran stars as Raya and Awkwafina as Sisu, in the film directed by Don Hall and Carlos López Estrada, and co-directed by Paul Briggs and John Ripa.</p>\n<p><em>Raya and the Last Dragon</em> releases on Digital today, <strong>April 2, 2021</strong> and 4K Ultra HD, Blu-ray, and DVD on <strong>May 18, 2021</strong>.</p>\n<p>See the bonus features offered with the home video releases below.</p>\n<p><strong><u>Walt Disney Animation Studios’ “Raya and the Last Dragon” Bonus Features*</u></strong></p>\n<ul>\n<li>An Introduction to “Us Again” – Director Zach Parrish takes you behind the scenes of the Walt Disney Animation Studios short.</li>\n<li>“Us Again” – An elderly man and his young-at-heart wife rekindle their passion for life on one magical night.</li>\n<li>Taste of Raya – Dine along with Kelly Marie Tran and the film’s creative team&#8211;virtually&#8211;over a Southeast Asian menu inspired by the countries that influenced the film as they discuss their experiences creating the world of Kumandra.</li>\n<li>Raya: Bringing it Home – When the global pandemic of 2020 hit, production of “Raya and the Last Dragon” moved to the houses of over 450 people. We open a window into their lives and learn how they overcame massive obstacles to make an animated feature from home.</li>\n<li>Martial Artists – Get a kick out of learning about the martial art forms and weapons used in the film as co-screenwriter Qui Nguyen and visual anthropologist Dr. S. Steve Arounsack share the inspiration behind the film’s action-packed elements.</li>\n<li>We are Kumandra – Meet members of the Southeast Asia Story Trust and discover the cultural influences that inspired the film&#8230;and how important this representation in a Disney animated film is to the people of the region.</li>\n<li>Outtakes – Step into the homes and behind the mics of the cast of “Raya and the Last Dragon” as they experience voice-over sessions in closets and shaky internet connections, which made recording this film unlike any other.</li>\n<li>Fun Facts &#38; Easter Eggs – Take a look at some of the hidden surprises and behind-the-scenes secrets of “Raya and the Last Dragon.”</li>\n<li>The Story Behind the Storyboard with John Ripa – Co-Director John Ripa invites you to get an inside look at his thought process as he pitches a storyboard sequence from the film and talks about his amazing career with Disney Animation.</li>\n<li>Deleted Scenes\n<ul>\n<li>Introduction – Head of Story Fawn Veerasunthorn introduces deleted scenes from “Raya and the Last Dragon.”</li>\n<li>The Bridge – Raya confronts an early version of the Druun in this deleted storyboard sequence.</li>\n<li>Escaping Namaari – See an early version sequence of an introduction to Namaari as an adult.</li>\n<li>Dragon Blade – Discover an early version of Raya’s sword, when it used to have magical powers.</li>\n<li>Meet Boun – Meet an early version of Boun before he was a chef and shrimp boat captain.</li>\n<li>The Heart of the Dragon – Co-Director John Ripa introduces a deleted scene which brought the theme of hope into the film.</li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n</ul>\n<p><img class=\"aligncenter size-medium wp-image-665201\" href=\"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/slashfilm?a=KBOuNYMbNbM:OHbAd16k8wI:yIl2AUoC8zA\"><img src=\"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/slashfilm?d=yIl2AUoC8zA\" border=\"0\"></img></a> <a +0000","feedId":21,"bgimg":"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/raya-and-the-last-dragon-5-700x293.jpg","linkMd5":"c75f29bc8bd655b5410d56cd48f7ad60","bgimgJsdelivr":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx8/cdn19@2020_4/2021/04/03/04-49-16-935_01db690ccb5a0b9b.webp","destWidth":700,"destHeight":293,"sourceBytes":22058,"destBytes":14462,"author":"Hoai-Tran Bui","articleImgCdnMap":{"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/raya-and-the-last-dragon-5-700x293.jpg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx8/cdn19@2020_4/2021/04/03/04-49-16-935_01db690ccb5a0b9b.webp","https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/raya-and-the-last-dragon-blu-ray-1-700x723.jpg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx29/cdn41@2020_5/2021/04/03/04-50-11-399_8e4b86e26a03d181.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/slashfilm?d=yIl2AUoC8zA":null,"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/slashfilm?i=KBOuNYMbNbM:OHbAd16k8wI:V_sGLiPBpWU":null,"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/slashfilm?d=I9og5sOYxJI":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx24/cdn57@2020_5/2021/04/03/04-50-11-348_879c5505f034c3d2.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/slashfilm?i=KBOuNYMbNbM:OHbAd16k8wI:EGzC5_Ws_ZE":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx11/cdn47@2020_5/2021/04/03/04-50-11-333_bc93ec75984cdd83.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~r/slashfilm/~4/KBOuNYMbNbM":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx25/cdn100@2020_4/2021/04/03/04-50-11-120_dfea297c321a862c.webp"},"publishedOrCreatedDate":1617425343656},{"createdTime":"2021-04-03 12:49:03","updatedTime":"2021-04-03 12:49:03","title":"James Cameron Almost Fired His ‘Avatar’ Sequel Writers’ Room","link":"https://www.slashfilm.com/?p=665124","description":"<p><a href=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/Avatar-sequel-writers-room.jpg\"><img class=\"aligncenter size-medium wp-image-665136\" src=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/Avatar-sequel-writers-room-700x321.jpg\" alt=\"Avatar sequel writers room\" width=\"700\" height=\"321\" srcset=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/Avatar-sequel-writers-room-700x321.jpg 700w, https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/Avatar-sequel-writers-room-360x165.jpg 360w, https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/Avatar-sequel-writers-room-768x352.jpg 768w, https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/Avatar-sequel-writers-room.jpg 948w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 700px) 100vw, 700px\" /></a></p>\n<p>Now that she&#8217;s no longer running for president, Marianne Williamson is spending her free time interviewing <strong>James Cameron</strong>. Williamson is a reported big fan of <strong><em>Avatar</em></strong>, and she recently spoke to <em>Avatar</em> grandaddy Cameron on <a href=\"https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=JdhWN-iG3eY&#38;t=2088s\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"nofollow noopener\">The Marianne Williamson Podcast.</a> There, the filmmaker dropped the surprising reveal that he came close to firing his <em>Avatar</em> sequel writers&#8217; room because the team was so focused on new stuff instead of obsessively combing over the things that made the first film such a success.</p>\n<p><span id=\"more-665124\"></span></p>\n<p><em>Avatar</em> is the biggest movie of all time, so James Cameron clearly knows a thing or two about a thing or two. Still, when I see him talking about his <em>Avatar</em> sequel writers&#8217; room, I get slightly concerned. During his conversation with Marianne Williamson (via <a href=\"https://www.indiewire.com/2021/04/james-cameron-threatened-fire-avatar-2-writers-1234627393/\">Indiewire</a>), Cameron said: &#8220;When I sat down to write the sequels, I knew there were going to be three at the time and eventually it turned into four, I put together a group of writers and said, ‘I don’t want to hear anybody’s new ideas or anyone’s pitches until we have spent some time figuring out what worked on the first film, what connected, and why it worked.'&#8221;</p>\n<p>I get what the filmmaker is going for here, but is there really some secret formula to explain the <em>Avatar</em> success? Isn&#8217;t it just likely that the film did so well because it featured advanced, cutting-edge technology that generated good word-of-mouth? And that the higher prices for 3D tickets helped inflate the box office haul? That seems to be the most reasonable explanation, but to hear Cameron tell it, there&#8217;s some sort of <em>Da Vinci Code</em>-like secret to <em>Avatar</em>&#8216;s record-breaking box office, and his writers needed to help him boil it down to its base elements.</p>\n<p>Cameron was <em>so</em> serious about this that he even threatened to fire everyone for not following his approach. &#8220;They kept wanting to talk about the new stories. I said, &#8216;We aren’t doing that yet.&#8217; Eventually I had to threaten to fire them all because they were doing what writers do, which is to try and create new stories. I said, ‘We need to understand what the connection was and protect it, protect that ember and that flame.'&#8221;</p>\n<p>Again: Cameron knows more about moviemaking than I do, so who am I to question this logic? And his writers work for him, so he has every right to fire them if he wants. Still, it seems weird that he was so dead-set against even discussing a new story. Cameron continued that he and the writing team sat down and rewatched the first movie together, and broke it down into a three-tier structure: tier one was &#8220;the surface storyline, which is just the plot,&#8221; tier two was &#8220;the spiritualism and the themes of capitalism, imperialism, colonialism, human rights abuses, and nature deficit disorder.&#8221; As for the third tier, that one is a bit more detailed:</p>\n<blockquote><p>&#8220;There was a tertiary level as well, and we were all in unison about it, but there was a level that was dreamlike that you could not express in a sentence. It didn’t have any ‘-isms’ to it, it was a dreamlike sense of a yearning to be there, to be in that space, to be in a place that is safe and where you wanted to be. Whether that was flying, that sense of freedom and exhilaration, or whether it’s being in the forest where you can smell the earth. It was a sensory thing that communicated on such a deep level. That was the spirituality of the first film.&#8221;</p></blockquote>\n<p>The big question now is: will this approach pay off? I guess we&#8217;ll find out when <em>Avatar 2</em> arrives on <strong>December 16, 2022</strong>.</p>\n<p>The post <a rel=\"nofollow\" href=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/avatar-sequel-writers-room/\">James Cameron Almost Fired His &#8216;Avatar&#8217; Sequel Writers&#8217; Room</a> appeared first on <a rel=\"nofollow\" href=\"https://www.slashfilm.com\">/Film</a>.</p>\n<div class=\"feedflare\">\n<a href=\"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/slashfilm?a=HOmTMM1Y_N4:vY37bLMPPIU:yIl2AUoC8zA\"><img
