Evangelista","articleImgCdnMap":{"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/Avatar-sequel-writers-room-700x321.jpg":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx27/cdn40@2020_5/2021/04/03/04-49-12-954_9db75934d33a4b9d.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/slashfilm?d=yIl2AUoC8zA":null,"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/slashfilm?i=HOmTMM1Y_N4:vY37bLMPPIU:V_sGLiPBpWU":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx7/cdn59@2020_6/2021/04/03/04-50-10-725_48f20c63a9da4cc4.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/slashfilm?d=I9og5sOYxJI":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx24/cdn57@2020_5/2021/04/03/04-50-11-348_879c5505f034c3d2.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/slashfilm?i=HOmTMM1Y_N4:vY37bLMPPIU:EGzC5_Ws_ZE":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx5oss/cdn36@2020_3/2021/04/03/04-50-10-506_c7d5dde5da3d82b5.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~r/slashfilm/~4/HOmTMM1Y_N4":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx33/cdn19@2020_1/2021/04/03/04-50-10-682_346b2ee3a45e9e36.webp"},"publishedOrCreatedDate":1617425343655},{"createdTime":"2021-04-03 12:49:03","updatedTime":"2021-04-03 12:49:03","title":"‘The Falcon and the Winter Soldier’ Team Up With Old Enemies and Lost Allies in “The Power Broker”","link":"https://www.slashfilm.com/?p=665167","description":"<p><img class=\"aligncenter wp-image-649832 size-medium\" src=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/Falcon-and-the-Winter-Soldier-TB-2-700x300.jpg\" alt=\"Falcon and the Winter Soldier The Power Broker Review\" width=\"700\" height=\"300\" srcset=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/Falcon-and-the-Winter-Soldier-TB-2.jpg 700w, https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/Falcon-and-the-Winter-Soldier-TB-2-360x154.jpg 360w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 700px) 100vw, 700px\" /></p>\n<p>Hello, and welcome to your weekly recap of <strong><em>The Falcon and the Winter Soldier</em></strong>. These are meant to be read after watching, so they will go deep into <strong>spoiler</strong> territory. You have been warned!</p>\n<p><span id=\"more-665167\"></span></p>\n<h2>Previously On…</h2>\n<p>In &#8220;The Star Spangled-Man,&#8221; Sam Wilson (<strong>Anthony Mackie</strong>) and Bucky Barnes (<strong>Sebastian Stan</strong>) fought the Flag Smashers in Munich alongside the new Captain America (<strong>Wyatt Russell)</strong> and Battlestar (<strong>Clé Bennett</strong>), but were unsuccessful in their attempt to recover the stolen Super Soldier Serum. Desperate for leads, Sam and Bucky decide to visit Baron Helmut Zemo (<strong>Daniel Brühl</strong>),the Sokovian Armed Forces Colonel turned terrorist responsible for creating the rift between Tony Stark and Steve Rogers in 2016’s <em>Captain America: Civil War.</em></p>\n<h2>A Message From Our Sponsor</h2>\n<p>Episode 3, &#8220;The Power Broker,&#8221; begins with a message from the Global Repatriation Council that feels a little bit like a prescription drug commercial and a lot like one of those insufferable &#8220;We&#8217;re here for you&#8221; ads you&#8217;ve seen a hundred times during the of COVID-19 pandemic:</p>\n<blockquote><p>&#8220;When half of us came back, it was time to rejoice and reunite. The Global Repatriation Council knows that for many it wasn&#8217;t that easy. So much has changed. But we&#8217;re here to help you find your way. Helping you back into your homes and jobs. Helping you navigate changes to society, laws, and borders. Helping you get back to the way things were. GRC, the Global Repatriation Council. Reset. Restore. Rebuild.&#8221;</p></blockquote>\n<h2>Red, White, and Brute</h2>\n<p>Back in Munich, the new Captain America is bustin&#8217; down the door of one of Karli Morgenthau&#8217;s (<strong>Erin Kellyman</strong>) allies, Rudy (<strong>Neal Kodinsky</strong>), the cafe owner seen in last week&#8217;s episode. &#8220;You Americans have become brutes,&#8221; he says, and he&#8217;s not wrong. John F. Walker&#8217;s Captain America is not Steve Rogers. Walker tries to interrogate Neil who refuses to answer his question and instead spits in his face. Walker roughs up the cafe owner and screams, &#8220;Do you know who I am?&#8221; to which the man responds, &#8220;Yes, I do. And I don&#8217;t care.&#8221;</p>\n<p>Outside, Battlestar attempts to reason with Walker. &#8220;Listen, she&#8217;s giving displaced people shelter and medicine,&#8221; he says. &#8220;That kinda thing creates loyalty, man. I know you want this. I get it. But we&#8217;ve literally tried everything we can here. So has Langley, and we keep drawin&#8217; blanks.&#8221;</p>\n<p>Having regained his composure, Walker knows he can&#8217;t do this without the help of some bonafide Avengers. &#8220;So we bet on someone who&#8217;s got a better hand.&#8221;</p>\n<h2>Machiavellian Machinations</h2>\n<p>In Berlin, at the headquarters of the Joint Counter Terrorist Centre, Sam and Bucky prepare to meet Zemo, but Bucky wants to go in alone. &#8220;You&#8217;re an Avenger,&#8221; Bucky says. &#8220;You know how he feels about that.&#8221;</p>\n<p>&#8220;It&#8217;s not like you two were known for frolicking in the sun together,&#8221; Sam replies.</p>\n<p>Bucky confronts Zemo, who&#8217;s in a cell fit for Hannibal Lecter. The terrorist steps out of the shadows and begins reciting the HYDRA code phrase that once controlled the Winter Soldier&#8217;s actions. &#8220;Longing. Rusted. Seventeen&#8230;&#8221;</p>\n<p>&#8220;Those days are over,&#8221; assures Bucky.</p>\n<p>&#8220;I know,&#8221; laments Zemo. &#8220;I just wanted to see how the new you reacts to the old words.&#8221;</p>\n<p>Bucky tells Zemo that someone has recreated the Super Soldier Serum. &#8220;You are assuming HYDRA has something to do with this, which is why you came to me, which means you are desperate,&#8221; he replies. &#8220;Luckily for you, I know where to begin.&#8221;</p>\n<p>Sam and Bucky need to break Zemo out of jail. They meet in a secluded location where Sam tries to reason with Bucky. &#8220;He blew up the U.N., he killed King T&#8217;Chaka and framed you for it. Did you forget that? You think the Wakandans forgot about it? It&#8217;s a rhetorical question. They didn&#8217;t.&#8221;</p>\n<p>Bucky walks Sam through a hypothetical scenario in which they spring Zemo. We&#8217;re taken step-by-step through a very elaborate plan only to discover that it&#8217;s already happened. &#8220;When Steve refused to sign the Sokovia Accords, you backed him,&#8221; says Bucky. &#8220;You broke the law, and you stuck your neck out for me. I&#8217;m asking you to do that again.&#8221;</p>\n<p>Zemo spent years hunting people HYDRA recruited to recreate the serum. &#8220;Because once it&#8217;s out there,&#8221; he warns, &#8220;someone can create an army of people&#8230; like the Avengers.&#8221; Zemo ended the Winter Soldier program once before and has no intention of leaving his work unfinished. To uncover the truth, they&#8217;ll have to scale a ladder of lowlifes. &#8220;First stop is a woman named Selby. Mid-level fence I still have a line on. From there, we climb.&#8221;</p>\n<h2>Welcome to Madripoor</h2>\n<p>Zemo, Sam, and Bucky take the Baron&#8217;s private jet to Madripoor, an island nation in the Indonesian archipelago. Divided between wealthy Hightown and impoverished, crime-ridden Lowtown, Madripoor is a haven for pirates and other criminals. Created by <strong>Chris Claremont</strong> and <strong>Steve Leialoha</strong>, the exotic locale made its Marvel Comics debut in 1985&#8217;s <em>New Mutants #32 </em>and was featured heavily in Claremont&#8217;s <em>Wolverine</em> series.</p>\n<p>During the flight, Zemo lectures Sam and Bucky on the dangers of hero-worship — a little bit of foreshadowing about what may become of John F. Walker&#8217;s Captain America.  He says that the danger with people like America&#8217;s Super Soldiers is that we put them on pedestals. &#8220;They become symbols. Icons. And then we start to forget about their flaws. From there, cities fly, innocent people die. Movements are formed, wars are fought.&#8221;</p>\n<p>Zemo, Bucky, and Sam — posing as an African rake named Conrad Mack, AKA the Smiling Tiger — make their way into the depths of Madripoor to meet Selby (<strong>Imelda Corcoran</strong>). Conrad Mack, by the way, was first introduced in 1992&#8217;s <em>New Warriors #19</em> as a mute feral being covered in orange fur and sharp claws. The offer is simple: Selby tells Zemo everything she knows about the Super Soldier Serum and she gets the Winter Soldier in return, along with the code words to control him, of course.</p>\n<p>As it turns out, the serum is in Madripoor, being developed by Dr. Wilfred Nagel (<strong>Olli Haaskivi</strong>) a character that first appeared in the 2003 series <em>Truth: Red, White &#38; Black </em>alongside Isaiah Bradley, the Black Captain America. Before the gang can get more information on Nagel&#8217;s location, the deal goes south and Selby is shot by Sharon Carter (<strong>Emily VanCamp</strong>). An enemy of the state, the great-niece of S.H.I.E.L.D. founder Peggy Carter has been hiding out on Madripoor, as the island nation doesn&#8217;t allow criminal extradition from within its borders.</p>\n<p>Carter isn&#8217;t ready to play Agent of S.H.I.E.L.D. again, however. &#8220;You know the whole hero thing is a joke, right? The way you gave up that shield, deep down, you must know it&#8217;s all hypocrisy.&#8221; When Bucky tries to interject, she scoffs, &#8220;Please. You buy into all that stars and stripes bullshit. Before you were his pet psychopath [pointing to Zemo], you were Mr. America! Cap&#8217;s best friend.&#8221;</p>\n<p>To quote Bucky, &#8220;Wow, she&#8217;s kind of awful now.&#8221;</p>\n<p>Sam makes a deal with Sharon. She helps them find Nagel and he&#8217;ll get her name cleared. Sharon, who is something of a hustler and art dealer, throws a party for her well-connected clients, leading to a pretty hilarious scene of Zemo cutting loose on the dance floor. During all the fun and frivolity, Sharon gets a lead on Nagel&#8217;s whereabouts and we&#8217;re off to the docks, where the gang uses a hidden doorway in an empty storage container to gain access to the scientist&#8217;s secret lab.</p>\n<p>As they begin to question Nagel, bounty hunters converge on the docks, leaving Sharon Carter to whip some serious ass. Back in the lab, we get a megalomaniacal monologue from Nagel that explains everything:</p>\n<blockquote><p>&#8220;I was brought into HYDRA&#8217;s Winter Soldier program to pick up their work after the five failed test subjects in Siberia. When HYDRA fell, I was recruited by the CIA. They had blood samples from an American test subject with semi-stable traces of serum in his system. After much labor, I was able to isolate the necessary compounds in his blood. I was a god. I did what no other scientist since Erskine was able to do. But mine was going to be different. No clunky machines or jacked-up bodies. Mine was going to be subtle, optimized, perfect.&#8221;</p></blockquote>\n<p>Using Isaiah Bradley&#8217;s blood, Nagel was able to recreate the serum. Before he was able to complete his work, however, he turned to dust during the Blip. When he returned five years later, the program had been abandoned, so he came to Madripoor. The mysterious Power Broker was more than happy to fund the continuation of his work. 20 vials were made, now in the possession of Karli Morgenthau. Once all the useful information is extracted from Nagel, Zemo shoots him dead. Way harsh, Helmut.</p>\n<h2>Wrappin&#8217; It Up</h2>\n<p>In Vilnius, Lithuania, we catch up with Karli and Dovich (<strong>Desmond Chiam</strong>) outside a GRC Supply Depot. The Global Repatriation Council has six months&#8217; worth of supplies sitting around collecting dust, so the Flag Smashers are stealing them and distributing them to the people who need them most.</p>\n<p>Meanwhile, in Berlin, Captain America and Battlestar are connecting the dots. Walker knows that Sam and Bucky broke Zemo out of prison, but as Battlestar points out, they can&#8217;t accuse them of something without evidence. &#8220;Which is why you and I are just gonna run with this one for a minute,&#8221; says Walker.</p>\n<p>Battlestar replies, &#8220;So I take what happens next isn&#8217;t a strictly on-the-books type thing, is it?&#8221;</p>\n<p>&#8220;Lemar,&#8221; Walker begins, &#8220;If we get the job done, you think they&#8217;re gonna sweat us on the how?&#8221;</p>\n<p>Zemo, Bucky, and Sam, meanwhile, make their way to Riga, Latvia, to search for Karli. Before they can get down to business, Bucky has a run-in with Ayo (<strong>Florence Kasumba</strong>), a member of the Dora Milaje — the personal bodyguards and royal security of the Black Panther. The warrior has only one thing to say. &#8220;I&#8217;m here for Zemo.&#8221;</p>\n<h2>Final Thoughts</h2>\n<p>&#8220;The Power Broker&#8221; is another strong episode of the Disney+ limited series created by <strong>Malcolm Spellman</strong> and directed by <strong>Kari Skogland</strong>. Mackie and Stan&#8217;s chemistry continues to be the selling point of the series, while it&#8217;s super-fun to see returning characters like Sharon Carter and Baron Zemo re-framed by the events of <em>Avengers: Infinity War</em> and <em>Avengers: Endgame</em>. They&#8217;re not in the same shape we left them in &#8211; they continue to develop alongside the major characters of the Marvel Cinematic Universe, which is nice to see. As for John F. Walker&#8217;s Captain America, I fully expect him to <span class=\"css-901oao css-16my406 r-poiln3 r-bcqeeo r-qvutc0\">get absolutely JUICED on some Super Soldier Serum and have a Battfleck-level </span><span class=\"css-901oao css-16my406 r-poiln3 r-b88u0q r-bcqeeo r-qvutc0\">roid</span><span class=\"css-901oao css-16my406 r-poiln3 r-bcqeeo r-qvutc0\"> rage episode where his mean streak is exposed to the world.</span></p>\n<p>For me, the real highlight of this episode is the introduction of Madripoor as yet another extremely cool locale for our heroes to explore. It&#8217;s the Mos Eisley Cantina of the Marvel Cinematic Universe — a wretched hive of scum and villainy that I can&#8217;t wait to see more of. It&#8217;s also a key location from the X-Men universe, which already has my gears spinning on how the MCU will bring Xavier&#8217;s mutants into the fold.</p>\n<p>What did you think of this week&#8217;s episode? Who is the mysterious Power Broker? Will we see Isaiah Bradley again? Will John F. Walker finally snap? And what will Ayo do when she gets her hands on Zemo? Join me next week for an in-depth breakdown of the latest episode!</p>\n<p>The post <a rel=\"nofollow\" 12:49:03","updatedTime":"2021-04-03 12:49:03","title":"‘What We Do in the Shadows’ Season 3 Teases a Returning Character and New Jackie Daytona-Inspired Directions","link":"https://www.slashfilm.com/?p=664816","description":"<p><img class=\"size-medium wp-image-619133 aligncenter\" src=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/what-we-do-in-the-shadows-season-3-700x321.jpg\" alt=\"What We Do in the Shadows Season 3\" width=\"700\" height=\"321\" srcset=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/what-we-do-in-the-shadows-season-3-700x321.jpg 700w, https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/what-we-do-in-the-shadows-season-3-360x165.jpg 360w, https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/what-we-do-in-the-shadows-season-3-768x352.jpg 768w, https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/what-we-do-in-the-shadows-season-3.jpg 948w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 700px) 100vw, 700px\" /></p>\n<p>It&#8217;s been far too long since we&#8217;ve spent time with our new favorite vampires in FX&#8217;s mockumentary series <strong><em>What We Do in the Shadows</em></strong>. Based on the film of the same name, the series follows a group of vampires living in the United States as they deal with the trials and tribulations of being bloodsuckers in the modern American world. With two seasons under its belt, the <em>What We Do in the Shadows</em> TV series has proven it&#8217;s every bit as good as the original movie, and it&#8217;s expanded the mythology of the series in an entertaining and creative way. But what&#8217;s in store for <em>What We do in the Shadows</em> season 3?<span id=\"more-664816\"></span></p>\n<p>The annual PaleyFest is unfolding in Los Angeles right now, celebrating the best TV shows on the air right now, and that includes a a tease of what&#8217;s to come on the next season of the Emmy-nominated <em>What We Do in the Shadows</em>. We&#8217;ve already heard that the third season will bring new creatures like <a href=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/what-we-do-in-the-shadows-season-3-comic-con-2020-panel/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">gargoyles and hellhounds into the fray</a>, but showrunner/executive producer <strong>Paul Simms</strong> and executive producer <strong>Stefani Robinson</strong> teased a returning character.</p>\n<p>Series regulars Nandor the Relentless (<strong>Kayvan Novak</strong>), his Familiar-turned-vampire-hunter Guillermo de la Cruz (<strong>Harvey Guillén</strong>), fellow vampires Laszlo Cravensworth (<strong>Matt Berry</strong>) and his lover Nadja (<strong>Natasia Demetriou</strong>), and energy vampire Colin Robinson (<strong>Mark Proksch</strong>) are all coming back. But Simms says they&#8217;ll be joined by a returning character who will be involved in a season-long arc. The showrunner only went so far as to say it&#8217;s <em>not</em> Nick Kroll as Simon the Devious, but it will be &#8220;someone we all know and love.&#8221;</p>\n<p>My initial hope was that we might see Jemaine Clement returning to <em>What We Do in the Shadows</em> in a major capacity. It doesn&#8217;t seem like he&#8217;s super busy with anything else right now, and bringing him into the show would be a lot of fun. He previously appeared as part of the Vampiric Council along with Taika Waititi and Jonathan Brugh as <em>What We Do in the Shadows</em> movie characters Viago von Dorna Schmarten Scheden Heimburg and Deacon Brucke, and it would make sense if he had to check in with the Staten Island bloodsuckers after the events of the second season. It could just as easily be Brugh stopping in too, but it&#8217;s unlikely to be Waititi since he&#8217;s very busy in production on <em>Thor: Love &#38; Thunder</em> and will be working on that movie for awhile.</p>\n<p>However, another potentially more interesting guess that would help expand the show&#8217;s narrative would be the return of Beanie Feldstein as Jenna, a college LARPer who was initially lured to the vampire clan by Guillermo as a delicious virgin feast. But in the first season, Jenna ended up being transformed into a vampire by Nadja after she saw the young girl wasn&#8217;t treated so well by her fellow students. Jenna was even learning how to hone her skills as a vampire, discovering she had the ability to become invisible. But we haven&#8217;t seen Jenna in quite some time, mostly <a href=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/what-we-do-in-the-shadows-season-2-guest-stars/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\">because of Feldstein&#8217;s movie schedule</a>, and bringing her back has a lot of potential. Maybe she&#8217;s even been around the whole time, just standing around being invisible.</p>\n<p>Unfortunately, there&#8217;s one character who we probably won&#8217;t see making a comeback anytime soon. Even though fans loved the second season debut of Jackie Daytona, a separate human character who definitely isn&#8217;t a disguise donned by vampire Laszlo Cravensworth, Simms and Robinson won&#8217;t be going back to that well anytime soon. But it did give them the confidence to take the show in even more surprising new directions. Robinson said:</p>\n<blockquote><p>&#8220;That episode gave us the opportunity to break format with all of the characters and push the show into new settings, formats, characters to explore what we’ve established. So not another Jackie Daytona adventure, but we have plans for the show to go into completely different directions.&#8221;</p></blockquote>\n<p>Simms and Robinson weren&#8217;t ready to reveal what those directions might be, but you can bet we&#8217;ll be ready when the time comes. Sadly, we&#8217;ll be waiting a long time before we get the third season. Production was intended to begin last month, but due to the ongoing coronavirus pandemic, production won&#8217;t begin until sometime later this year, which means we probably won&#8217;t see the show return until late in 2021 and possibly not until early 2022.</p>\n<p>The post <a rel=\"nofollow\" href=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/what-we-do-in-the-shadows-season-3-hints/\">&#8216;What We Do in the Shadows&#8217; Season 3 Teases a Returning Character and New Jackie Daytona-Inspired Directions</a> appeared first on <a rel=\"nofollow\" href=\"https://www.slashfilm.com\">/Film</a>.</p>\n<div 12:49:03","updatedTime":"2021-04-03 12:49:03","title":"‘Black Panther 2’ Director Ryan Coogler Says Chadwick Boseman “Wouldn’t Have Wanted Us To Stop”","link":"https://www.slashfilm.com/?p=664846","description":"<p><a href=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/black-panther-2-update.jpg\"><img class=\"aligncenter size-medium wp-image-664870\" src=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/black-panther-2-update-700x321.jpg\" alt=\"black panther 2 update\" width=\"700\" height=\"321\" srcset=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/black-panther-2-update-700x321.jpg 700w, https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/black-panther-2-update-360x165.jpg 360w, https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/black-panther-2-update-768x352.jpg 768w, https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/black-panther-2-update.jpg 948w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 700px) 100vw, 700px\" /></a></p>\n<p><strong>Chadwick Boseman</strong>&#8216;s death last summer caught almost everyone off-guard as the actor had kept his colon cancer diagnosis private. And <strong>Ryan Coogler</strong>, who directed Boseman in <em>Black Panther</em>, was one of the many people surprised by Boseman&#8217;s death, as he had already been working on the script for <strong><em>Black Panther 2</em></strong> for Boseman to star in. Following Boseman&#8217;s passing, there was some question as to how the film series could even continue. Eventually, everyone decided to move forward with altered plans – <em>Black Panther 2</em> would happen, but rather than recast Boseman&#8217;s now-iconic role of T&#8217;Challa, Coogler would re-work his script. In a recent interview, Coogler adds that moving forward would&#8217;ve been exactly what Boseman would&#8217;ve wanted.</p>\n<p><span id=\"more-664846\"></span></p>\n<p>The quote from Ryan Coogler about <em>Black Panther 2</em> comes from <a href=\"https://www.hollywoodreporter.com/features/judas-and-the-black-messiahs-all-black-team-on-bittersweet-feeling-of-making-oscar-history\">THR</a>, where the filmmaker opened up a bit about having to continue on with the film in the wake of Chadwick Boseman&#8217;s unexpected death. &#8220;I didn&#8217;t know what was going on,&#8221; Coogler said in regards to Boseman&#8217;s illness. &#8220;I knew what he wanted me to know. I miss him in every way that you could miss somebody, as a friend, as a collaborator. And it sucks because I love watching movies, and I don&#8217;t get to watch the next thing he would have made. So it&#8217;s grief on a lot of levels, but then, it&#8217;s a deep sense of gratitude because I can close my eyes and hear his voice.&#8221;</p>\n<p>After Boseman&#8217;s death many wondered how, exactly, <em>Black Panther 2</em> would continue. Would Coogler and Marvel recast the lead role? The answer turned out to be no – rather than bring in a new actor to play T&#8217;Challa, Coogler is instead reworking the script. It&#8217;s not entirely clear how this will all work out – the most popular assumption is that the film will shift focus to <strong>Letitia Wright</strong> as T&#8217;Challa&#8217;s sister Shuri, but that&#8217;s just speculation for the time being.</p>\n<p>However things pan out, Coogler made it clear that giving up in the wake of Boseman&#8217;s death was not an option. &#8220;You’ve got to keep going when you lose loved ones. I know Chad wouldn’t have wanted us to stop,&#8221; the director said. &#8220;He was somebody who was so about the collective. <em>Black Panther</em>, that was his movie. He was hired to play that role before anybody else was even thought of, before I was hired, before any of the actresses were hired. On that set, he was all about everybody else. Even though he was going through what he was going through, he was checking in on them, making sure they were good. If we cut his coverage, he would stick around and read lines off-camera [to help other actors with their performances]. So it would be harder for me to stop. Truthfully. I&#8217;d feel him yelling at me, like, &#8216;What are you doing?&#8217; So you keep going.&#8221;</p>\n<p><em>Black Panther 2</em> is currently set to open on <strong>July 22, 2022</strong>.</p>\n<p>The post <a rel=\"nofollow\" href=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/black-panther-2-update/\">&#8216;Black Panther 2&#8217; Director Ryan Coogler Says Chadwick Boseman 12:49:03","updatedTime":"2021-04-03 12:49:03","title":"‘Us Again’ Clip: Get a Taste of Disney’s Theatrical Short Attached to ‘Raya and the Last Dragon’","link":"https://www.slashfilm.com/?p=665208","description":"<p><img class=\"size-medium wp-image-665216 aligncenter\" src=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/usagain-couple-dancing-nyc-700x300.jpg\" alt=\"Us Again Clip\" width=\"700\" height=\"300\" srcset=\"https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/usagain-couple-dancing-nyc.jpg 700w, https://www.slashfilm.com/wp/wp-content/images/usagain-couple-dancing-nyc-360x154.jpg 360w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 700px) 100vw, 700px\" /></p>\n<p>On top of missing the theatrical movie-going experience altogether over the past year, it&#8217;s been a bummer to miss out on Disney&#8217;s tradition of including animated short films before their big screen releases. Thankfully, the short film attached to the theatrical release of <strong><em>Raya and the Last Dragon</em></strong> is coming home with the movie&#8217;s digital release today.</p>\n<p><strong><em>Us Again</em></strong> is written and directed by <strong>Zach Parrish</strong>, who served as head of animation on <em>Big Hero 6</em> and will be at the helm of an animated <em>Short Circuit</em> movie at Disney. The film follows an elderly couple as they joyously rekindle their youth through the magic of dancing, and a little <em>Us Again</em> clip gives us a taste of the fancy footwork that will take us through the city.<span id=\"more-665208\"></span></p>\n<h2>Us Again Clip</h2>\n<p><iframe width=\"740\" height=\"416\" src=\"https://www.youtube.com/embed/1n-gCLoBSTU?feature=oembed\" frameborder=\"0\" allow=\"accelerometer; autoplay; clipboard-write; encrypted-media; gyroscope; picture-in-picture\" allowfullscreen></iframe></p>\n<blockquote><p>Set in a vibrant city pulsating with rhythm and movement, an elderly man and his young-at-heart wife rekindle their youthful passion for life and each other on one magical night. The years fade away as the joy of dancing propels them across the exciting cityscape of their youth and revives fond memories and ambitions.</p></blockquote>\n<p>If they used the characters from Pixar&#8217;s <em>Up</em>, then they could have called this movie <em>Up Again</em>. (It&#8217;s okay, I&#8217;ll see myself out).</p>\n<p>Anyway, this clip is so vibrant and full of life, and the animation looks phenomenal too. The rain-soaked city looks beautiful at night, and the dance moves are crisp and clean as a lively score pulses in the background. There&#8217;s plenty more dancing to behold too, with horeographers/dancers <strong>Keone &#38; Mari Madrid</strong> (champions of the dance competition series <em>World of Dance</em>) providing the moves for this short film. The score comes from <em>Captain Marvel</em> composer <strong>Pinar Toprak</strong>.</p>\n<p>The only way to see <em>Us Again</em> previously was if you saw <em>Raya and the Last Dragon</em> in theaters. But when you pick up the movie on home video (including <span class=\"ILfuVd NA6bn\"><span class=\"hgKElc\">4K Ultra HD, Blu-ray and DVD on May 18)</span></span>, it will be included as a special feature. If you&#8217;re not planning on picking up the movie for your collection, you&#8217;ll still have another shot at seeing <em>Us Again</em> when it arrives on Disney+ sometime in June, joining the rest of the Disney and Pixar short films that have been released in theaters over the years. It&#8217;s just a shame more people won&#8217;t have a chance to see it on the big screen.</p>\n<p>You can still see <em>Us Again</em> in theaters right now with <em>Raya and the Last
